# Task: Kubernetes client-go Systems Guide

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce an advanced systems guide for client-go that explains API access, controller loops, and extension paths.

## Scope

Focus on the client-go subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

     1→# `client-go` Architecture
     2→
     3→This document explains the internal architecture of `client-go` for contributors. It describes the
     4→major components, how they interact, and the key design decisions that shape the library.
     5→
     6→## Client Configuration
     7→
     8→There is an architectural separation between loading client configuration and using it. The
     9→`rest.Config` object is the in-memory representation of this configuration. The
    10→`tools/clientcmd` package is the standard factory for producing it. `clientcmd` handles the
    11→complex logic of parsing `kubeconfig` files, merging contexts, and handling external
    12→authentication providers (e.g., OIDC).
    13→
    14→## REST Client
    15→
    16→The `rest.Client` is the foundational HTTP client that underpins all other clients. It separates
    17→the low-level concerns of HTTP transport, serialization, and error handling from higher-level,
    18→Kubernetes-specific object logic.
    19→
    20→The `rest.Config` object is used to build the underlying HTTP transport, which is typically a
    21→chain of `http.RoundTripper` objects. Each element in the chain is responsible for a specific
    22→task, such as adding an `Authorization` header. This is the mechanism by which all authentication
    23→is injected into requests.
    24→
    25→The client uses a builder pattern for requests (e.g., `.Verb()`, `.Resource()`), deferring
    26→response processing until a method like `.Into(&pod)` is called. This separation is key to
    27→supporting different client models from a common base.
    28→
    29→### Endpoint Interactions
    30→
    31→*   **Content Negotiation:** The client uses HTTP `Accept` headers to negotiate the wire format
    32→    (JSON or Protobuf). A 
... (truncated)

     1→> ⚠️ **This is an automatically published [staged repository](https://git.k8s.io/kubernetes/staging#external-repository-staging-area) for Kubernetes**.   
     2→> Contributions, including issues and pull requests, should be made to the main Kubernetes repository: [https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes](https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes).  
     3→> This repository is read-only for importing, and not used for direct contributions.  
     4→> See [CONTRIBUTING.md](./CONTRIBUTING.md) for more details.
     5→
     6→# client-go
     7→
     8→Go clients for talking to a [kubernetes](http://kubernetes.io/) cluster.
     9→
    10→We recommend using the `v0.x.y` tags for Kubernetes releases >= `v1.17.0` and
    11→`kubernetes-1.x.y` tags for Kubernetes releases < `v1.17.0`.
    12→
    13→The fastest way to add this library to a project is to run `go get k8s.io/client-go@latest` with go1.16+.
    14→See [INSTALL.md](/INSTALL.md) for detailed installation instructions and troubleshooting.
    15→

// Store is a generic object storage and processing interface.  A
// Store holds a map from string keys to accumulators, and has
// operations to add, update, and delete a given object to/from the
// accumulator currently associated with a given key.  A Store also
// knows how to extract the key from a given object, so many operations
// are given only the object.
//
// In the simplest Store implementations each accumulator is simply
// the last given object, or empty after Delete, and thus the Store's
// behavior is simple storage.
//
// Reflector knows how to watch a server and update a Store.  This
// package provides a variety of implementations of Store.
type Store interface {

	// Add adds the given object to the accumulator associated with the given object's key
	Add(obj interface{}) error

	// Update updates the given object in the accumulator associated with the given object's key
	Update(obj interface{}) error

	// Delete deletes the given object from the accumulator associated with the given object's key
	Delete(obj interface{}) error

	// List returns a list of 
... (truncated)

	// Touch can be hooked when an existing item is added again. This may be

	// Push adds a new item.
	Push(item T)
	// Len tells the total number of items.
	Len() int
	// Pop retrieves an item.
	Pop() (item T)
}

// Indexer extends Store with multiple indices and restricts each
// accumulator to simply hold the current object (and be empty after
// Delete).
//
// There are three kinds of strings here:
//  1. a storage key, as defined in the Store interface,
//  2. a name of an index, and
//  3. an "indexed value", which is produced by an IndexFunc and
//     can be a field value or any other string computed from the object.
type Indexer interface {
	Store
	// Index returns the stored objects whose set of indexed values
	// intersects the set of indexed values of the given object, for
	// the named index
	Index(indexName string, obj interface{}) ([]interface{}, error)
	// IndexKeys returns the storage keys of the stored objects whose
	// set of indexed values for the named index includes the given
	// indexed value
	IndexKeys(indexName, indexedValue string) ([]string, error)
	// ListIndexFuncValues returns all the indexed values of the given index
	ListIndexFuncValues(indexName string) []string
	// ByIndex returns the stored objects whose set of indexed values
	// for the named index includes the given indexed val
... (truncated)

// Package leaderelection implements leader election of a set of endpoints.
// It uses an annotation in the endpoints object to store the record of the
// election state. This implementation does not guarantee that only one
// client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).
//
// A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the
// leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader
// election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been
// produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their
// accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has
// renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary
// clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.
//
// However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting
// RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a
// maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on
// the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets
// the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted
// to tolerate some nodes progr
... (truncated)

**Location:** `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/`

```

│   ├── clientcmd/            # Kubeconfig parsing & client config

│   ├── pager/                # List pagination

│   ├── flowcontrol/          # Rate limiting

    26→// TypedRateLimitingInterface is an interface that rate limits items being added to the queue.
    27→type TypedRateLimitingInterface[T comparable] interface {
    28→	TypedDelayingInterface[T]
    29→
    30→	// AddRateLimited adds an item to the workqueue after the rate limiter says it's ok
    31→	AddRateLimited(item T)
    32→
    33→	// Forget indicates that an item is finished being retried.  Doesn't matter whether it's for perm failing
    34→	// or for success, we'll stop the rate limiter from tracking it.  This only clears the `rateLimiter`, you
    35→	// still have to call `Done` on the queue.
    36→	Forget(item T)
    37→
    38→	// NumRequeues returns back how many times the item was requeued
    39→	NumRequeues(item T) int
    40→}
    41→
    42→// RateLimitingQueu
... (truncated)

# Kubernetes Client-Go Systems Guide

## Executive Summary

Client-go is the canonical Go client library for interacting with Kubernetes clusters. It implements a layered architecture that provides both synchronous REST client access and asynchronous event-driven caching with reconciliation loops. The library balances type safety (through code generation), runtime flexibility (through dynamic clients), and operational efficiency (through smart caching and rate limiting).

This guide covers the architectural foundations, component interactions, extension mechanisms, and operational considerations for understanding how client-go works and where extension points exist.

---

## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies

### Purpose

Client-go enables Go applications to:
- **Create, read, update, delete (CRUD)** Kubernetes API objects
- **Watch** for changes in real-time
- **Cache** objects locally with event-driven synchronization
- **Coordinate** multiple replicas using distributed locks
- **Discover** supported API groups, versions, and resources

### Subsystem Boundaries

**Upstream Dependencies:**
- **k8s.io/apimachinery**: Provides runtime object serialization, error types, and core interfaces (Store, Watch, Reflector patterns)
- **k8s.io/api**: Kubernetes API type definitions (Pod, Deployment, etc.)
- **HTTP/2 RoundTripper**: Standard Go net/http for transport layer

**Downstream Consumers:**
- Controllers (in-tree and out-of-tree)
- Operators and custom resources
- CLI tools (kubectl, krew plugins)
- Webhooks and webhook servers
- Custom reconciliation loops

**Critical Boundary Distinction:**
Client-go is **not a control plane** and makes no decisions about cluster state. It is purely a client library for interacting with a
... (truncated)

### 7.9 Code Generation

| Component | Location | Purpose |
|-----------|----------|---------|
| Clientset Generator | (external: k8s.io/code-generator) | Generate `kubernetes/` clients |
| Informer Generator | (external: k8s.io/code-generator) | Generate `informers/` factory |

| Apply Config Generator | (external: k8s.io/code-generator) | Generate `applyconfigurations/` |
| Fake Client Generator | (external: k8s.io/code-generator) | Generate fake clients for testing |

---

## 8. Summary

**Client-go Architecture**:
1. **Foundation**: REST client with rate limiting and backoff
2. **Type Safety**: Code-generated clients for all Kubernetes APIs
3. **Efficiency**: Cached informers with event-driven synchronization
4. **Operational**: Work queues, rate limiting, leader election
5. **Flexibility**: Dynamic and metadata clients for untyped access

**Key Strengths**:
- Eventual consistency guarantees simplify controller logic
- Event-driven reconciliation prevents polling overhead
- Code generation ensures API server/client alignment
- Work queues enable robust error handling

**Key Constraints**:
- Informers have startup cost (LIST all objects)
- Cache eventual consistency window
- Resync overhead on large object counts
- Requires idempotent reconciliation logic

**When to Use**:
- **Typed Client**: Bui

Main Components and Packages\n\n#### **A. REST Client (`rest/` package)**\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `rest/client.go` - RESTClient interface and implementation\n- `rest/config.go` - Config struct (authentication, TLS, rate limiting)\n- `rest/request.go` - Request builder pattern implementation\n- `rest/transport.go` - HTTP transport setup\n- `rest/with_retry.go` - Retry logic\n\n**Purpose:** Foundational HTTP client underpinning all other clients. Provides low-level REST API interaction.\n\n**Key Interface:**\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    GetRateLimiter() flowcontrol.RateLimiter\n    Verb(verb string) *Request\n    Post() *Request\n    Put() *Request\n    Patch(pt types.PatchType) *Request\n    Get() *Request\n    Delete() *Request\n    APIVersion() schema.GroupVersion\n}\n```\n\n**Key Features:**\n- Builder pattern for requests (`.Verb()`, `.Resource()`, `.Into()`)\n- Content negotiation (JSON, Protobuf, PartialObjectMetadata)\n- Rate limiting (QPS and Burst settings)\n- Server-side throttling (Retry-After headers)\n- Backoff management\n- Authentication chain via RoundTripper middleware\n- Structured error handling (StatusError)\n- Streaming watch support\n\n---\n\n#### **B. Typed Clientset (`kubernetes/` package)**\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `kubernetes/clientset.go` - Main Clientset interface (code-generated)\n- `kubernetes/typed/` - Per-API-group typed clients (code-generated)\n- `kubernetes/scheme/` - Runtime scheme registration\n\n**Purpose:** Compile-time type-safe access to core Kubernetes APIs.\n\n**Structure:**\nThe clientset is organized by API groups and versions:\n- `kubernetes/typed/core/v1/` - Core v1 API\n- `kubernetes/typed/apps/v1/` - Apps v1 API\n- `kubernetes/typed/batch/v1/` - Batch v1 API\n- `kubernetes/typed/admissionregistration/v1/` - Admission registration\n- etc. (26+ API groups supported)\n\n**Typical Usage Pattern:**\n```go\nclientset, _ := kubernetes.NewForConfig(config)\npods, _ := clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").List(ctx, metav1.ListOptions{})\n```\n\n---\n\n#### **C. Informers (`informers/` package)**\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `informers/factory.go` - SharedInformerFactory (code-generated)\n- `informers/[group]/[version]/` - Per-type informers (code-generated)\n- `informers/internalinterfaces/` - Internal interfaces\n\n**Purpose:** Machinery for populating caches with event-driven synchronization from API server.\n\n**Key Concepts:**\n- **SharedInformerFactory**: Coordinates all informers and manages resource versioning\n- **SharedIndexInformer**: Individual informer for a specific type\n- **TweakListOptions**: Customize LIST/WATCH queries\n- **Resync Period**: Periodic cache reconciliation\n\n**Architecture:**\n```\nAPI Server (LIST/WATCH)\n    \u2193\nReflector (watches changes)\n    \u2193\nDeltaFIFO (queues deltas)\n    \u2193\nIndexer/Cache (stores objects with indexes)\n    \u2193\nEvent Handlers (triggers callbacks)\n    \u2193\nWork Queue (queues keys for controller processing)\n```\n\n---\n\n#### **D. Listers (`listers/` package)**\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `listers/[group]/[version]/[resource].go` - Per-resource listers (code-generated)\n- `listers/expansion.go` - Interface for custom methods\n\n**Purpose:** Read-only, thread-safe cache accessors for controller business logic.\n\n**Pattern:**\n```go\ntype DeploymentLister interface {\n    List(selector labels.Selector) ([]*appsv1.Deployment, error)\n    Deployments(namespace string) DeploymentNamespaceLister\n}\n\ntype DeploymentNamespaceLister interface {\n    List(selector labels.Selector) ([]*appsv1.Deployment, error)\n    Get(name string) (*appsv1.Deployment, error)\n}\n```\n\n**Characteristics:**\n- Uses indexes for efficient queries\n- Supports label selectors\n- Namespace-scoped and cluster-wide\n- Generated from API types\n\n---\n\n#### **E. Dynamic Client (`dynamic/` package)**\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `dynamic/interface.go` - Dynamic client interface\n- `dynamic/simple.go` - Implementation\n- `dynamic/scheme.go` - Scheme handling\n- `dynamic/dynamicinformer/` - Dynamic informers\n- `dynamic/dynamiclister/` - Dynamic listers\n\n**Purpose:** Unstructured/generic client for working with any Kubernetes resource (including CRDs).\n\n**Key Interface:**\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    Resource(resource schema.GroupVersionResource) NamespaceableResourceInterface\n}\n\ntype ResourceInterface interface {\n    Create(ctx context.Context, obj *unstructured.Unstructured, ...) (*unstructured.Unstructured, error)\n    Update(ctx context.Context, obj *unstructured.Unstructured, ...) (*unstructured.Unstructured, error)\n    Delete(ctx context.Context, name string, ...) error\n    Get(ctx context.Context, name string, ...) (*unstructured.Unstructured, error)\n    List(ctx context.Context, opts metav1.ListOptions) (*unstructured.UnstructuredList, error)\n    Watch(ctx context.Context, opts metav1.ListOptions) (watch.Interface, error)\n    Patch(ctx context.Context, name string, pt types.PatchType, ...) (*unstructured.Unstructured, error)\n    Apply(ctx context.Context, name string, obj *unstructured.Unstructured, ...) (*unstructured.Unstructured, error)\n}\n```\n\n**Characteristics:**\n- Works with any resource (built-in or custom)\n- Uses discovery to determine API paths\n- Supports CRDs and custom resources\n- Includes dynamic informers and listers\n\n---\n\n#### **F. Metadata Client (`metadata/` package)**\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `metadata/interface.go` - Metadata client interface\n- `metadata/metadata.go` - Implementation\n- `metadata/metadatainformer/` - Metadata informers\n- `metadata/metadatalister/` - Metadata listers\n\n**Purpose:** Lightweight client for working only with object metadata (PartialObjectMetadata).\n\n**Key Interface:**\n```go\ntype ResourceInterface interface {\n    Delete(ctx context.Context, name string, ...) error\n    DeleteCollection(ctx context.Context, ...) error\n    Get(ctx context.Context, name string, ...) (*metav1.PartialObjectMetadata, error)\n    List(ctx context.Context, opts metav1.ListOptions) (*metav1.PartialObjectMetadataList, error)\n    Watch(ctx context.Context, opts metav1.ListOptions) (watch.Interface, error)\n    Patch(ctx context.Context, name string, pt types.PatchType, ...) (*metav1.PartialObjectMetadata, error)\n}\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Efficient label selection\n- Garbage collection\n- Watch/sync with minimal bandwidth\n- Metadata-only operations\n\n---\n\n### 3. Key Interfaces and Types\n\n#### **A. Cache/Store Interfaces (`tools/cache/`)**\n\n**Store Interface:**\n```go\ntype Store interface {\n    Add(obj interface{}) error\n    Update(obj interface{}) error\n    Delete(obj interface{}) error\n    List() []interface{}\n    ListKeys() []string\n    Get(obj interface{}) (item interface{}, exists bool, err error)\n    GetByKey(key string) (item interface{}, exists bool, err error)\n    Replace([]interface{}, string) error\n    Resync() error\n}\n```\n\n**Indexer Interface:**\n```go\ntype Indexer interface {\n    Store\n    Index(indexName string, obj interface{}) ([]interface{}, error)\n    IndexKeys(indexName, indexedValue string) ([]string, error)\n    ListIndexFuncValues(indexName string) []string\n    ByIndex(indexName, indexedValue string) ([]interface{}, error)\n    GetIndexers() Indexers\n    AddIndexers(newIndexers Indexers) error\n}\n```\n\n**Key Implementations:**\n- `cache` - Basic in-memory store\n- `DeltaFIFO` - Queue with object deltas (Add/Update/Delete/Sync)\n- `Heap` - Priority queue for expiration-based caching\n\n---\n\n#### **B. Reflector (`tools/cache/reflector.go`)**\n\n**Purpose:** Performs LIST to get snapshot, then WATCH for continuous updates.\n\n**Key Methods:**\n- `Run()` - Starts the reflector\n- `ListAndWatch()` - LIST/WATCH loop with recovery from \"too old\" resource version errors\n- Handles watch bookmarks for recovery\n\n---\n\n#### **C. Controller (`tools/cache/controller.go`)**\n\n**Config Structure:**\n```go\ntype Config struct {\n    Queue               // DeltaFIFO for queuing\n    ListerWatcher       // LIST/WATCH source\n    Process ProcessFunc // Callback for processing deltas\n    FullResyncPeriod time.Duration\n    // ... error handlers, watch timeout, etc.\n}\n```\n\n**Pattern:** Low-level controller used by SharedInformer.\n\n---\n\n#### **D. Work Queue (`util/workqueue/`)**\n\n**TypedInterface:**\n```go\ntype TypedInterface[T comparable] interface {\n    Add(item T)\n    Len() int\n    Get() (item T, shutdown bool)\n    Done(item T)\n    ShutDown()\n    ShutDownWithDrain()\n    ShuttingDown() bool\n}\n```\n\n**Key Features:**\n- FIFO queue\n- Rate limiting with exponential backoff\n- Duplicate prevention\n- Metrics integration\n\n**Critical Boundary:**\n- Informers add keys to work queue\n- Controllers process keys with retry logic\n- Decouples event detection from reconciliation\n\n---\n\n#### **E. REST Mapper (`restmapper/`)**\n\n**Purpose:** Maps GroupVersionResources and GroupVersionKinds to REST API paths.\n\n**Uses Discovery** to determine:\n- Which resources exist\n- Whether resources are namespaced\n- API groups and versions\n- Preferred versions\n\n---\n\n#### **F. Discovery Client (`discovery/`)**\n\n**Key Responsibilities:**\n- List supported API groups and versions\n- Describe resources in each API group\n- Fetch OpenAPI schemas\n- Cache results (CachedDiscoveryClient)\n\n---\n\n#### **G. Leader Election (`tools/leaderelection/`)**\n\n**Purpose:** Enable single-writer semantics across replicas using a Lease object.\n\n**Key Pattern:**\n- Multiple replicas compete for Lease lock\n- Lease has LeaseDuration (how long lock is held)\n- RenewDeadline (time before trying to renew)\n- Only one replica acts as leader at a time\n\n---\n\n### 4. Patterns and Flows for API Interaction\n\n#### **Pattern 1: Direct REST Client Usage**\n\n```go\n// Low-level API interaction\nconfig := rest.InClusterConfig()\nclientset, _ := kubernetes.NewForConfig(config)\npods, _ := clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").List(ctx, metav1.ListOptions{})\n```\n\n**Characteristics:**\n- One-off requests\n- No caching\n- Direct API calls\n- Suitable for initial setup\n\n---\n\n#### **Pattern 2: Informer-Based Event Handling**\n\n```\n1. Create SharedInformerFactory\n2. For each resource type:\n   a. Get informer from factory\n   b. Add event handlers (AddEventHandler)\n   c. Get lister from informer for reads\n3. Start factory (starts all informers)\n4. In event handler: add object key to work queue\n5. In controller loop: get key from queue, use lister to read, reconcile\n```\n\n**Flow:**\n```\nInformer (background):\n  Reflector \u2192 LIST to snapshot, WATCH for updates\n  \u2193\n  DeltaFIFO \u2192 Queue deltas\n  \u2193\n  Indexer \u2192 Store with indexes\n  \u2193\n  Event Handlers \u2192 Trigger callbacks\n\nUser Code (controller):\n  Event Handler \u2192 Add key to WorkQueue\n  \u2193\n  Controller Loop:\n    - Get key from queue\n    - Get object via Lister\n    - Reconcile\n    - Mark Done, requeue on error with backoff\n```\n\n---\n\n#### **Pattern 3: Dynamic Client for Untyped Resources**\n\n```go\n// Works with CRDs or any resource\ndynamicClient := dynamic.NewForConfigOrDie(config)\nunstructuredObj := &unstructured.Unstructured{...}\nresult, _ := dynamicClient.Resource(gvr).Namespace(\"default\").Create(ctx, unstructuredObj, ...)\n```\n\n**Characteristics:**\n- No compile-time type checking\n- Flexible for extensibility\n- Uses discovery for API paths\n- Works with any resource\n\n---\n\n#### **Pattern 4: REST Config Building**\n\n```go\n// From kubeconfig file\nconfig, _ := clientcmd.BuildConfigFromFlags(\"\", \"/home/user/.kube/config\")\n\n// From in-cluster (running in Pod)\nconfig, _ := rest.InClusterConfig()\n\n// Manual construction\nconfig := &rest.Config{\n    Host: \"https://kubernetes.default.svc\",\n    BearerToken: \"...\",\n    TLSClientConfig: rest.TLSClientConfig{CAFile: \"/var/run/secrets/...\"},\n}\n\n// Build clients from config\nclientset, _ := kubernetes.NewForConfig(config)\ndynamicClient, _ := dynamic.NewForConfig(config)\ndiscoveryClient, _ := discovery.NewDiscoveryClientForConfig(config)\n```\n\n---\n\n#### **Pattern 5: Leader Election**\n\n```go\nleaderelection.RunOrDie(ctx, leaderelection.LeaderElectionConfig{\n    Lock: &resourcelock.LeaseLock{\n        Client: coordinationV1Client,\n        LockConfig: resourcelock.ResourceLockConfig{\n            Identity: podName,\n        },\n    },\n    LeaseDuration: 15 * time.Second,\n    RenewDeadline: 10 * time.Second,\n    RetryPeriod:   2 * time.Second,\n    Callbacks: leaderelection.LeaderCallbacks{\n        OnStartedLeading: func(ctx context.Context) { /* run controller */ },\n        OnStoppedLeading: func() { /* cleanup */ },\n    },\n})\n```\n\n---\n\n#### **Pattern 6: Server-Side Apply (Declarative Updates)**\n\n```go\n// Uses type-safe apply configurations (code-generated)\napplyConfig := appsv1apply.Deployment(...).\n    WithSpec(appsv1apply.DeploymentSpec().\n        WithReplicas(3).\n        ...)\n\nclientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").Apply(ctx, applyConfig, metav1.ApplyOptions{...})\n```\n\n**Key Difference from CRUD:**\n- Declarative: specify what state should be\n- Multi-controller safe: multiple controllers can manage same object\n- Server-side merging of changes\n\n---\n\n### 5. Key Internal Packages\n\n| Package | Purpose |\n|---------|---------|\n| `tools/cache` | Caching, indexing, reflector, controller coordination |\n| `tools/clientcmd` | Kubeconfig parsing and client config building |\n| `tools/leaderelection` | Distributed lock implementation |\n| `tools/record` | Event recording to API server |\n| `tools/watch` | Watch stream utilities |\n| `util/workqueue` | Threaded work queue with rate limiting |\n| `util/flowcontrol` | Token bucket rate limiting |\n| `util/retry` | Retry utilities |\n| `transport` | HTTP/2 transport setup, auth middleware |\n| `restmapper` | Resource/kind to REST path mapping |\n| `discovery` | API discovery client |\n| `plugin/pkg/client/auth` | Authentication plugins (OIDC, exec, etc.) |\n\n---\n\n### 6. Code Generation\n\nClient-go heavily uses code generation from `k8s.io/code-generator`:\n\n**Generated Components:**\n- **Clientsets** - Type-safe clients for each API group/version\n- **Informers** - SharedInformer factories for each type\n- **Listers** - Read-only cache accessors\n- **Apply Configurations** - Type-safe apply builders\n- **Fake Clients** - For testing\n\n**Location:** Most files in `kubernetes/`, `informers/`, `listers/`, and `applyconfigurations/` are generated with header:\n```go\n// Code generated by client-gen. DO NOT EDIT.\n```\n\n---\n\n### 7. Architecture Highlights\n\n**1. Layered Design:**\n- HTTP Transport Layer (RoundTripper chain)\n- REST Client Layer (builders, verb/resource)\n- Typed Client Layer (clientsets)\n- Dynamic Client Layer (unstructured)\n- Informer/Cache Layer (event-driven, indexed)\n\n**2. Content Negotiation:**\n- Supports JSON, Protobuf, CBOR\n- Can request PartialObjectMetadata (metadata-only)\n- Can request Table format for lists\n\n**3. Error Handling:**\n- Structured StatusError (programmatic inspection)\n- Warnings from API server\n- Backoff and retry logic\n- Rate limit respect (429 responses)\n\n**4. Performance Optimizations:**\n- Shared caches via informers\n- Indexes for efficient queries\n- Watch bookmarks for recovery\n- List pagination\n- Content negotiation (Protobuf for bandwidth)\n\n**5. Extensibility:**\n- RoundTripper middleware chain for auth\n- Index functions for custom queries\n- Event handler callbacks\n- Work queue for custom reconciliation logic\n- Plugin system for authentication\n\n---\n\n### Summary\n\n**Client-go** provides a comprehensive Go client library for interacting with Kubernetes APIs. It implements both **typed** (compile-safe) and **dynamic** (flexible) access patterns, with sophisticated **caching and event-driven** mechanisms for building controllers. The architecture cleanly separates concerns across REST transport, client generation, caching, and reconciliation layers, making it suitable for both simple API interactions and complex operator/controller development.\n\nThe library's design emphasizes:\n- **Type Safety** through code generation\n- **Efficiency** through smart caching and indexing\n- **Resilience** through retry logic and leader election\n- **Extensibility** through middleware and callbacks\n- **Clarity** through consistent interfaces and patterns",

"     1\u2192# `client-go` Architecture\n     2\u2192\n     3\u2192This document explains the internal architecture of `client-go` for contributors. It describes the\n     4\u2192major components, how they interact, and the key design decisions that shape the library.\n     5\u2192\n     6\u2192## Client Configuration\n     7\u2192\n     8\u2192There is an architectural separation between loading client configuration and using it. The\n     9\u2192`rest.Config` object is the in-memory representation of this configuration. The\n    10\u2192`tools/clientcmd` package is the standard factory for producing it. `clientcmd` handles the\n    11\u2192complex logic of parsing `kubeconfig` files, merging contexts, and handling external\n    12\u2192authentication providers (e.g., OIDC).\n    13\u2192\n    14\u2192## REST Client\n    15\u2192\n    16\u2192The `rest.Client` is the foundational HTTP client that underpins all other clients. It separates\n    17\u2192the low-level concerns of HTTP transport, serialization, and error handling from higher-level,\n    18\u2192Kubernetes-specific object logic.\n    19\u2192\n    20\u2192The `rest.Config` object is used to build the underlying HTTP transport, which is typically a\n    21\u2192chain of `http.RoundTripper` objects. Each element in the chain is responsible for a specific\n    22\u2192task, such as adding an `Authorization` header. This is the mechanism by which all authentication\n    23\u2192is injected into requests.\n    24\u2192\n    25\u2192The client uses a builder pattern for requests (e.g., `.Verb()`, `.Resource()`), deferring\n    26\u2192response processing until a method like `.Into(&pod)` is called. This separation is key to\n    27\u2192supporting different client models from a common base.\n    28\u2192\n    29\u2192### Endpoint Interactions\n    30\u2192\n    31\u2192*   **Content Negotiation:** The client uses HTTP `Accept` headers to negotiate the wire format\n    32\u2192    (JSON or Protobuf). A key performance optimization using this mechanism is the ability to\n    33\u2192    request metadata-only objects via the `as=PartialObjectMetadata;g=meta.k8s.io;v=v1` Accept custom parameter.\n    34\u2192    Also the `as=Table;g=meta.k8s.io;v=v1` Accept custom parameters may be used to request lists as tables. \n    35\u2192*   **Subresources:** The client can target standard subresources like `/status` or `/scale` for\n    36\u2192    object mutations, and it can also handle action-oriented subresources like `/logs` or\n    37\u2192    `/exec`, which often involve streaming data.\n    38\u2192*   **List Pagination:** For `LIST` requests, the client can specify a `limit`. The server will\n    39\u2192    return up to that many items and, if more exist, a `continue` token. The client is\n    40\u2192    responsible for passing this token in a subsequent request to retrieve the next page.\n    41\u2192    Higher-level tools like the `Reflector`'s `ListerWatcher` handle this logic automatically.\n    42\u2192*   **Streaming Watches:** A `WATCH` request returns a `watch.Interface` (from\n    43\u2192    `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/watch`), which provides a channel of structured `watch.Event`\n    44\u2192    objects (`ADDED`, `MODIFIED`, `DELETED`, `BOOKMARK`). This decouples the watch consumer from\n    45\u2192    the underlying streaming protocol.\n    46\u2192\n    47\u2192### Errors, Warnings, and Rate Limiting\n    48\u2192\n    49\u2192*   **Structured Errors:** The client deserializes non-2xx responses into a structured\n    50\u2192    `errors.StatusError`, enabling programmatic error handling (e.g., `errors.IsNotFound(err)`).\n    51\u2192*   **Warnings:** It processes non-fatal `Warning` headers from the API server via a\n    52\u2192    `WarningHandler`.\n    53\u2192*   **Client-Side Rate Limiting:** The `QPS` and `Burst` settings in `rest.Config` are the\n    54\u2192    client's half of the contract with the server's API Priority and Fairness system.\n    55\u2192*   **Server-Side Throttling:** The client's default transport automatically handles HTTP `429`\n    56\u2192    responses by reading the `Retry-After` header, waiting, and retrying the request.\n    57\u2192\n    58\u2192## Typed and Dynamic Clients\n    59\u2192\n    60\u2192To handle the extensible nature of the Kubernetes API, `client-go` provides two primary client\n    61\u2192models.\n    62\u2192\n    63\u2192The **`kubernetes.Clientset`** provides compile-time, type-safe access to core, built-in APIs.\n    64\u2192\n    65\u2192The **`dynamic.DynamicClient`** represents all objects as `unstructured.Unstructured`, allowing it\n    66\u2192to interact with any API resource, including CRDs. It relies on two discovery mechanisms:\n    67\u21921.  The **`discovery.DiscoveryClient`** determines *what* resources exist. The\n    68\u2192    **`CachedDiscoveryClient`** is an optimization that caches this data on disk to solve.\n    69\u21922.  The **OpenAPI schema** (fetched from `/openapi/v3`) describes the *structure* of those\n    70\u2192    resources, providing the schema awareness needed by the dynamic client.\n    71\u2192\n    72\u2192## Code Generation\n    73\u2192\n    74\u2192A core architectural principle of `client-go` is the use of code generation to provide a\n    75\u2192strongly-typed, compile-time-safe interface for specific API GroupVersions. This makes\n    76\u2192controller code more robust and easier to maintain. The tools in `k8s.io/code-generator` produce\n    77\u2192several key components:\n    78\u2192\n    79\u2192*   **Typed Clientsets:** The primary interface for interacting with a specific GroupVersion.\n    80\u2192*   **Typed Listers:** The read-only, cached accessors used by controllers.\n    81\u2192*   **Typed Informers:** The machinery for populating the cache for a specific type.\n    82\u2192*   **Apply Configurations:** The type-safe builders for Server-Side Apply.\n    83\u2192\n    84\u2192A contributor modifying a built-in API type **must** run the code generation scripts to update all\n    85\u2192of these dependent components. For the Kubernetes project, `hack/update-codegen.sh` runs code generation.\n    86\u2192\n    87\u2192`sample-controller` shows how code generate can be configured to build custom controllers.\n    88\u2192\n    89\u2192## Controller Infrastructure\n    90\u2192\n    91\u2192The `tools/cache` package provides the core infrastructure for controllers, replacing a high-load,\n    92\u2192request-based pattern with a low-load, event-driven, cached model.\n    93\u2192\n    94\u2192The data flow is as follows:\n    95\u2192\n    96\u2192```mermaid\n    97\u2192graph TD\n    98\u2192    subgraph \"Kubernetes API\"\n    99\u2192        API_Server[API Server]\n   100\u2192    end\n   101\u2192\n   102\u2192    subgraph \"client-go: Informer Mechanism\"\n   103\u2192        Reflector(\"1. Reflector\")\n   104\u2192        DeltaFIFO(\"2. DeltaFIFO\")\n   105\u2192        Indexer[\"3. Indexer (Cache)\"]\n   106\u2192        EventHandlers(\"4. Event Handlers\")\n   107\u2192    end\n   108\u2192\n   109\u2192    subgraph \"User Code\"\n   110\u2192        WorkQueue[\"5. Work Queue\"]\n   111\u2192        Controller(\"6. Controller\")\n   112\u2192    end\n   113\u2192\n   114\u2192    API_Server -- LIST/WATCH --> Reflector\n   115\u2192    Reflector -- Puts changes into --> DeltaFIFO\n   116\u2192    DeltaFIFO -- Is popped by internal loop, which updates --> Indexer\n   117\u2192    Indexer -- Update triggers --> EventHandlers\n   118\u2192    EventHandlers -- Adds key to --> WorkQueue\n   119\u2192    WorkQueue -- Is processed by --> Controller\n   120\u2192    Controller -- Reads from cache via Lister --> Indexer\n   121\u2192```\n   122\u2192\n   123\u2192A **`Reflector`** performs a `LIST` to get a consistent snapshot of a resource, identified by a\n   124\u2192`resourceVersion`. It then starts a `WATCH` from that `resourceVersion` to receive a continuous\n   125\u2192stream of subsequent changes. The `Reflector`'s relist/rewatch loop is designed to solve the\n   126\u2192**\"too old\" `resourceVersion` error** by re-listing. To make this recovery more efficient, the\n   127\u2192`Reflector` consumes **watch bookmarks** from the server, which provide a more recent\n   128\u2192`resourceVersion` to restart from.\n   129\u2192\n   130\u2192The **`Lister`** is the primary, read-only, thread-safe interface for a controller's business\n   131\u2192logic to access the `Indexer`'s cache.\n   132\u2192\n   133\u2192## Controller Patterns\n   134\u2192\n   135\u2192The controller infrastructure is architecturally decoupled from the controller's business logic to\n   136\u2192ensure resiliency.\n   137\u2192\n   138\u2192The **`util/workqueue`** creates a critical boundary between event detection (the informer's job)\n   139\u2192and reconciliation (the controller's job). Informer event handlers only add an object's key to the\n   140\u2192work queue. This allows the controller to retry failed operations with exponential backoff without\n   141\u2192blocking the informer's watch stream.\n   142\u2192\n   143\u2192For high availability, the **`tools/leaderelection`** package provides the standard architectural\n   144\u2192solution to ensure single-writer semantics by having replicas compete to acquire a lock on a\n   145\u2192shared `Lease` object.\n   146\u2192\n   147\u2192## Server-Side Apply\n   148\u2192\n   149\u2192`client-go` provides a distinct architectural pattern for object mutation that aligns with the\n   150\u2192server's declarative model. This is a separate workflow from the traditional `get-modify-update`\n   151\u2192model that allows multiple controllers to safely co-manage the same object. The\n   152\u2192**`applyconfigurations`** package provides the generated, type-safe builder API used to\n   153\u2192construct the declarative patch.\n   154\u2192\n   155\u2192## Versioning and Compatibility\n   156\u2192\n   157\u2192`client-go` has a strict versioning relationship with the main Kubernetes repository. A `client-go`\n   158\u2192version `v0.X.Y` corresponds to the Kubernetes version `v1.X.Y`.\n   159\u2192\n   160\u2192The Kubernetes API has strong backward compatibility guarantees: a client built with an older\n   161\u2192version of `client-go` will work with a newer API server. However, the reverse is not guaranteed.\n   162\u2192A contributor must not break compatibility with supported versions of the Kubernetes API server.\n   163\u2192\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. You CAN and SHOULD provide analysis of malware, what it is doing. But you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code. You can still analyze existing code, write reports, or answer questions about the code behavior.\n</system-reminder>\n"

PRs that are\n    50\u2192cherry-picked into an older Kubernetes release branch will result in an update\n    51\u2192to the corresponding branch in `client-go`, with a corresponding new tag\n    52\u2192changing the patch version.\n    53\u2192\n    54\u2192#### Branches and tags.\n    55\u2192\n    56\u2192We will create a new branch and tag for each increment in the minor version\n    57\u2192number. We will create only a new tag for each increment in the patch\n    58\u2192version number. See [semver](http://semver.org/) for definitions of major,\n    59\u2192minor, and patch.\n    60\u2192\n    61\u2192The HEAD of the master branch in client-go will track the HEAD of the master\n    62\u2192branch in the main Kubernetes repo.\n    63\u2192\n    64\u2192#### Compatibility: your code <-> client-go\n    65\u2192\n    66\u2192The `v0.x.y` tags indicate that go APIs may change in incompatible ways in\n    67\u2192different versions.\n    68\u2192\n    69\u2192See [INSTALL.md](INSTALL.md) for guidelines on requiring a specific\n    70\u2192version of client-go.\n    71\u2192\n    72\u2192#### Compatibility: client-go <-> Kubernetes clusters\n    73\u2192\n    74\u2192Since Kubernetes is backwards compatible with clients, older `client-go`\n    75\u2192versions will work with many different Kubernetes cluster versions.\n    76\u2192\n    77\u2192We will backport bugfixes--but not new features--into older versions of\n    78\u2192`client-go`.\n    79\u2192\n    80\u2192\n        | +-              | +-              | +-              | +-              | +-              |\n    92\u2192\n    93\u2192Key:\n    94\u2192\n    95\u2192* `\u2713` Exactly the same features / API objects in both client-go and the Kubernetes\n    96\u2192  version.\n    97\u2192* `+` client-go has features or API objects that may not be present in the\n    98\u2192  Kubernetes cluster, either due to that client-go has additional new API, or\n    99\u2192  that the server has removed old API. However, everything they have in\n   100\u2192  common (i.e., most APIs) will work. Please note that alpha APIs may vanish or\n   101\u2192  change significantly in a single release.\n   102\u2192* `-` The Kubernetes cluster has features the client-go library can't use,\n   103\u2192  either due to the server has additional new API, or that client-go has\n   104\u2192  removed old API. However, everything they share in common (i.e., most APIs)\n   105\u2192  will work.\n   106\u2192\n   107\u2192See the [CHANGELOG](./CHANGELOG.md) for a detailed description of changes\n   108\u2192between client-go versions.\n   109\u2192\n   110\u2192| Branch         | Canonical source code location      | Maintenance status |\n   111\u2192| -------------- | ----------------------------------- | ------------------ |\n   112\u2192| `release-1.25` | Kubernetes main repo, 1.25 branch   | =-                 |\n   113\u2192| `release-1.26` | Kubernetes main repo, 1.26 branch   | =-                 |\n   114\u2192| `release-1.27` | Kubernetes main repo, 1.27 branch   | =-                 |\n   115\u2192| `release-1.28` | Kubernetes main repo, 1.28 branch   | =-                 |\n   116\u2192| `release-1.29` | Kubernetes main repo, 1.29 branch   | =-                 |\n   117\u2192| `release-1.30` | Kubernetes main repo, 1.30 branch   | =-                 |\n   118\u2192| `release-1.31` | Kubernetes main repo, 1.31 branch   | =                  |\n   119\u2192| `release-1.32` | Kubernetes main repo, 1.32 branch   | \u2713                  |\n   120\u2192| `release-1.33` | Kubernetes main repo, 1.33 branch   | \u2713                  |\n   121\u2192| `release-1.34` | Kubernetes main repo, 1.34 branch   | \u2713                  |\n   122\u2192| client-go HEAD | Kubernetes main repo, master branch | \u2713                  |\n   123\u2192\n   124\u2192Key:\n   125\u2192\n   126\u2192* `\u2713` Changes in main Kubernetes repo are actively published to client-go by a bot\n   127\u2192* `=` Maintenance is manual, only severe security bugs will be patched.\n   128\u2192* `-` Deprecated; please upgrade.\n   129\u2192\n   130\u2192#### Deprecation policy\n   131\u2192\n   132\u2192We will maintain branches for at least six months after their first stable tag\n   133\u2192is cut. (E.g., the clock for the release-2.0 branch started ticking when we\n   134\u2192tagged v2.0.0, not when we made the first alpha.) This policy applies to\n   135\u2192every version greater than or equal to 2.0.\n   136\u2192\n   137\u2192#### Why do the 1.4 and 1.5 branch contain top-level folder named after the version?\n   138\u2192\n   139\u2192For the initial release of client-go, we thought it would be easiest to keep\n   140\u2192separate directories for each minor version. That soon proved to be a mistake.\n   141\u2192We are keeping the top-level folders in the 1.4 and 1.5 branches so that\n   142\u2192existing users won't be broken.\n   143\u2192\n   144\u2192### Kubernetes tags\n   145\u2192\n   146\u2192This repository is still a mirror of\n   147\u2192[k8s.io/kubernetes/staging/src/client-go](https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/tree/master/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go),\n   148\u2192the code development is still done in the staging area.\n   149\u2192\n   150\u2192Since Kubernetes `v1.8.0`, when syncing the code from the staging area,\n   151\u2192we also sync the Kubernetes version tags to client-go, prefixed with\n   152\u2192`kubernetes-`. From Kubernetes `v1.17.0`, we also create matching semver\n   153\u2192`v0.x.y` tags for each `v1.x.y` Kubernetes release.\n   154\u2192\n   155\u2192For example, if you check out the `kubernetes-1.17.0` or the `v0.17.0` tag in\n   156\u2192client-go, the code you get is exactly the same as if you check out the `v1.17.0`\n   157\u2192tag in Kubernetes, and change directory to `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go`.\n   158\u2192\n   159\u2192The purpose is to let users quickly find matching commits among published repos,\n   160\u2192like [sample-apiserver](https://github.com/kubernetes/sample-apiserver),\n   161\u2192[apiextension-apiserver](https://github.com/kubernetes/apiextensions-apiserver),\n   162\u2192etc. The Kubernetes version tag does NOT claim any backwards compatibility\n   163\u2192guarantees for client-go. "/*\nCopyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\n\nLicensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\nyou may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\nYou may obtain a copy of the License at\n\n    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n\nUnless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\ndistributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\nWITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\nSee the License for the specific language governing permissions and\nlimitations under the License.\n*/\n\n// Package leaderelection implements leader election of a set of endpoints.\n// It uses an annotation in the endpoints object to store the record of the\n// election state. This implementation does not guarantee that only one\n// client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\n//\n// A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\n// leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\n// election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\n// produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\n// accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\n// renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\n// clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\n//\n// However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\n// RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\n// maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\n// the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\n// the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\n// to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n// the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n//\n// While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n// cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\n// this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\n// availability.\n//\n// Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\n// taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\n// should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\n// until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\n// when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\n// to master availability.\n//\n// DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This library will likely change significantly\n// or even be removed entirely in subsequent releases. It is used to decide which items are missing\n\t// when Replace() is called; 'Deleted' deltas are produced for the missing items.\n\t// KnownObjects may be nil if you can tolerate missing deletions on Replace().\n\tKnownObjects KeyListerGetter\n\n\t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced indicates that the queue consumer\n\t// understands the Replaced DeltaType. Before the `Replaced` event type was\n\t// added, calls to Replace() were handled the same as Sync(). For\n\t// backwards-compatibility purposes, this is false by default.\n\t// When true, `Replaced` events will be sent for items passed to a Replace() call.\n\t// When false, `Sync` events will be sent instead.\n\tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\n\n\t// If set, will be called for objects before enqueueing them. Please\n\t// see the comment on TransformFunc for details.\n\tTransformer TransformFunc\n\n\t// If set, log output will go to this logger instead of klog.Background().\n\tLogger *klog.Logger\n}\n\n// DeltaFIFO is like FIFO, but differs in two ways.  One is that the\n// accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\n// but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\n// object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\n// except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\n// Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\n// not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\n// Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\n// DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\n//\n// The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\n// an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\n// If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\n// replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\n// resync events.\n//\n// DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\n// intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\n// the Pop() method.\n//\n// DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\n//   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\n//   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\n//     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\n//   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\n//   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\n//\n// DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\n// interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\n// will always return an object of type Deltas. List() returns\n// the newest object from each accumulator in the FIFO.\n//\n// A DeltaFIFO's knownObjects KeyListerGetter provides the abilities\n// to list Store keys and to get objects by Store key.  The objects in\n// question are called \"known objects\" and this set of objects\n// modifies the behavior of the Delete, Replace, and Resync methods\n// (each in a different way).\n//\n// A note on threading: If you call Pop() in parallel from multiple\n// threads, you could end up with multiple threads processing slightly\n// different versions of the same object.\ntype DeltaFIFO struct {\n\t// lock/cond protects access to 'items' and 'queue'.\n\tlock sync.RWMutex\n\tcond sync.Cond\n\n\t// `items` maps a key to a Deltas.\n\t// Each such Deltas has at least one Delta.\n\titems map[string]Deltas\n\n\t// `queue` maintains FIFO order of keys for consumption in Pop().\n\t// There are no duplicates in `queue`.\n\t// A key is in `queue` if and only if it is in `items`.\n\tqueue []string\n\n\t// populated is true if the first batch of items inserted by Replace() has been populated\n\t// or Delete/Add/Update/AddIfNotPresent was called first.\n\tpopulated bool\n\t// initialPopulationCount is the number of items inserted by the first call of Replace()\n\tinitialPopulationCount int\n\n\t// keyFunc is used to make the key used for queued item\n\t// insertion and retrieval, and should be deterministic.\n\tkeyFunc KeyFunc\n\n\t// knownObjects list keys that are \"known\" --- affecting Delete(),\n\t// Replace(), and Resync()\n\tknownObjects KeyListerGetter\n\n\t// Used to indicate a queue is closed so a control loop can exit when a queue is empty.\n\t// Currently, not used to gate any of CRUD operations.\n\tclosed bool\n\n\t// emitDeltaTypeReplaced is whether to emit the Replaced or Sync\n\t// DeltaType when Replace() is called (to preserve backwards compat).\n\temitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\n\n\t// Called with every object if non-nil.\n\ttransformer TransformFunc\n\n\t// logger is a per-instance logger. An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\n// namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\n// an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\n// SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\n// group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\n// SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\n// applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\n//\n// The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\n// access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\n// An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\n// other appropriate content or (2) \"absent\".\n//\n// A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\n// by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\n// machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\n// the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\n// consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\n// prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\n// particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\n// then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\n// eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\n// state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\n// service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\n// absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\n// selector.\n//\n// For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\n// states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\n// states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\n// might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\n// states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\n// ordering between states seen for different objects.\n//\n// The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\n// during `Run()`.\n//\n// As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\n// unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\n// collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\n// SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\n// collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\n// service ends, or communication problems between the two\n// persistently thwart achievement).\n//\n// As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\n// non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\n// removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\n// removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\n// too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\n// problems persistently thwart the desired result).\n//\n// The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\n// objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\n// Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\n// a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\n// into its constituent parts.\n//\n// Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\n// snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\n// will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\n//\n// A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\n// update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\n// added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\n// stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\n// after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\n// additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\n// client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\n// local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\n// SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\n// update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\n// update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\n// corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\n// and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\n// For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\n// delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\n// object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\n// `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\n// that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\n// `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\n// and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\n// created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\n// rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\n// need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\n// field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\n// notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\n//\n// A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\n// is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\n// notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\n// to something else, for example through a\n// `client-go/util/workqueue`.\n//\n// A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\n// state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\n// ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\ntype SharedInformer interface {\n\t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\n\t// the shared informer's resync period.
