50. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# Kubernetes Client-Go Systems Guide\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nClient-go is the canonical Go client library for interacting with Kubernetes clusters. It implements a layered architecture that provides both synchronous REST client access and asynchronous event-driven caching with reconciliation loops. The library balances type safety (through code generation), runtime flexibility (through dynamic clients), and operational efficiency (through smart caching and rate limiting).\n\nThis guide covers the architectural foundations, component interactions, extension mechanisms, and operational considerations for understanding how client-go works and where extension points exist.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nClient-go enables Go applications to:\n- **Create, read, update, delete (CRUD)** Kubernetes API objects\n- **Watch** for changes in real-time\n- **Cache** objects locally with event-driven synchronization\n- **Coordinate** multiple replicas using distributed locks\n- **Discover** supported API groups, versions, and resources\n\n### Subsystem Boundaries\n\n**Upstream Dependencies:**\n- **k8s.io/apimachinery**: Provides runtime object serialization, error types, and core interfaces (Store, Watch, Reflector patterns)\n- **k8s.io/api**: Kubernetes API type definitions (Pod, Deployment, etc.)\n- **HTTP/2 RoundTripper**: Standard Go net/http for transport layer\n\n**Downstream Consumers:**\n- Controllers (in-tree and out-of-tree)\n- Operators and custom resources\n- CLI tools (kubectl, krew plugins)\n- Webhooks and webhook servers\n- Custom reconciliation loops\n\n**Critical Boundary Distinction:**\nClient-go is **not a control plane** and makes no decisions about cluster state. It is purely a client library for interacting with an existing API server. Control decisions happen in controllers that consume client-go's events and issue write operations.\n\n### Key Design Principles\n\n1. **Layered Architecture**: REST foundation, typed clients on top, informer machinery as a higher abstraction\n2. **Eventual Consistency**: Caches are eventually consistent with the authoritative API server state\n3. **Event-Driven Reconciliation**: Controllers respond to changes via events, not polling\n4. **Thread-Safe by Contract**: Informers guarantee sequential event delivery to handlers; controllers use work queues for concurrent processing\n5. **Multiple Access Patterns**: Synchronous (direct REST), asynchronous (informers + work queues), dynamic (unstructured resources)\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibilities\n\n### 2.1 REST Client Foundation (`rest/`)\n\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/rest/`\n\n**Responsibility**: Foundational HTTP client providing low-level REST API interaction.\n\n**Key Types**:\n- **`Config`** (`rest/config.go`): Holds authentication, TLS, rate limiting, and server connection details\n  - Supports Bearer tokens, Basic auth, client certificates, OIDC, exec-based auth\n  - Default QPS: 5.0, Burst: 10 (tunable)\n  - Impersonation headers for admin operations\n\n- **`RESTClient`** (`rest/client.go`): Implements the request builder pattern\n  - Single entry point for all REST operations\n  - Manages rate limiting and backoff\n  - Negotiates content types (JSON, Protobuf, PartialObjectMetadata)\n\n- **`Request`** (`rest/request.go`): Builder pattern for constructing API requests\n  - Chain methods: `.Resource()`, `.Name()`, `.Namespace()`, `.Subresource()`\n  - Example: `client.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-pod\", metav1.GetOptions{})`\n  - Supports streaming watches, error handling with structured `StatusError`\n\n**Rate Limiting**: Via `flowcontrol.RateLimiter` interface\n- Token bucket implementation\n- QPS and Burst configurable per config\n- Respects server-sent `Retry-After` headers\n- Exponential backoff on 500-level errors\n\n**Design Trade-off**: Direct REST calls have no caching\u2014suitable for one-off operations but inefficient for controllers.\n\n---\n\n### 2.2 Typed Clientset (`kubernetes/`)\n\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes/`\n\n**Responsibility**: Compile-time type-safe access to all Kubernetes API groups and versions.\n\n**Architecture**:\n```\nclientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"ns\").Get(...)    // Type-safe\nclientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"ns\").List(...)\nclientset.BatchV1().Jobs(\"ns\").Watch(...)\n```\n\n**Generated Structure** (`kubernetes/typed/[group]/[version]/`):\n- Per-API-group clients (CoreV1, AppsV1, BatchV1, etc. \u2014 26+ groups)\n- Per-resource interfaces (PodInterface, DeploymentInterface, etc.)\n- Per-resource implementations with REST path logic\n- Fake clients for testing\n\n**Code Generation**: All clientset code is generated from API types by `k8s.io/code-generator`\n- Header: `// Code generated by client-gen. DO NOT EDIT.`\n- Generated on each Kubernetes release\n- Ensures client and server APIs stay in sync\n\n**Expansion Interfaces** (`kubernetes/typed/[group]/[version]/generated_expansion.go`):\n- Extension points for adding custom methods to generated clients\n- Example: `DeploymentNamespaceListerExpansion` for custom queries\n\n**Design Trade-off**: Type safety at compile time prevents entire classes of runtime errors, but requires code generation for new API groups.\n\n---\n\n### 2.3 Informers and Caching (`tools/cache/`)\n\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/`\n\n**Responsibility**: Machinery for populating local caches from the API server with event-driven synchronization.\n\n**Core Components**:\n\n#### 2.3.1 Reflector (`tools/cache/reflector.go`)\n\n**Pattern**: Watches a resource and pushes changes into a store.\n\n**Algorithm**:\n1. **Initial LIST**: Fetch all objects at a starting `resourceVersion`\n2. **WATCH Loop**: Subscribe to changes at that resource version\n3. **Detect \"Too Old\"**: If watch stream indicates the resource version is stale, restart with a new LIST\n4. **Backoff**: Exponential backoff on connection errors\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `Run()`: Starts the reflector in a goroutine\n- `ListAndWatch()`: Implements the LIST/WATCH protocol\n- `LastSyncResourceVersion()`: Current sync state (thread-safe)\n\n**Pagination Support**:\n- `WatchListPageSize`: Can paginate large LIST operations\n- Trade-off: Direct etcd access is slower but uses fewer server resources\n\n**Design Feature**: Watch bookmarks allow recovery without expensive re-LIST operations\n\n---\n\n#### 2.3.2 DeltaFIFO Queue (`tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`)\n\n**Pattern**: Producer-consumer queue that accumulates deltas (changes) for each object.\n\n**Key Concept**: Deltas, not full objects\n```go\ntype Deltas []Delta\ntype Delta struct {\n    Type   DeltaType  // Added, Updated, Deleted, Replaced, Sync\n    Object interface{}\n}\n```\n\n**Why Deltas?**\n- Batches rapid changes to the same object into one entry\n- Preserves deletion information (full object state before deletion)\n- Tracks whether object was replaced (UID changed)\n- Periodic resync via \"Sync\" delta for reconciliation\n\n**Producer**: Reflector calls `Add()`, `Update()`, `Delete()`, `Replace()`\n**Consumer**: Controller calls `Pop()` to get next delta\n\n**Resync Behavior**:\n- Periodic reconciliation via `Replace()` \u2192 generates \"Sync\" deltas\n- Full resync period configurable per informer (default 15 minutes)\n- Optional: emit \"Replaced\" delta type for server-side apply scenarios\n\n**Thread-Safe**: Uses mutex internally; parallel Pop() calls possible but discouraged (can process different versions of same object)\n\n---\n\n#### 2.3.3 Indexer (`tools/cache/store.go`)\n\n**Pattern**: In-memory, indexed storage for fast queries.\n\n**Interfaces**:\n```go\ntype Store interface {\n    Add(obj interface{}) error\n    Update(obj interface{}) error\n    Delete(obj interface{}) error\n    Get(obj interface{}) (item interface{}, exists bool, err error)\n    List() []interface{}\n}\n\ntype Indexer interface {\n    Store\n    Index(indexName string, obj interface{}) ([]interface{}, error)\n    ByIndex(indexName, indexedValue string) ([]interface{}, error)\n    AddIndexers(newIndexers Indexers) error\n}\n```\n\n**Index Functions**: Custom mappings from object \u2192 query keys\n- Example: `PodByOwnerIndexFunc` indexes pods by their owner reference\n- Used for efficient lookups: \"Get all pods owned by this deployment\"\n\n**Implementation**: `cache` (basic in-memory map)\n\n---\n\n#### 2.3.4 SharedInformer (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go`)\n\n**Pattern**: High-level coordination of Reflector, DeltaFIFO, Indexer, and event distribution.\n\n**Responsibilities**:\n1. Creates and starts a Reflector and DeltaFIFO queue\n2. Maintains an Indexer (read-only cache)\n3. Manages list of event handlers\n4. Guarantees sequential delivery to each handler\n5. Provides \"started\" signal for controllers to wait on\n\n**Key Interface**:\n```go\ntype SharedInformer interface {\n    AddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\n    GetStore() Store\n    GetIndexer() Indexer\n    HasSynced() bool  // True once initial LIST is complete\n    LastSyncResourceVersion() string\n}\n```\n\n**Event Handler Contract**:\n- `OnAdd(obj interface{})`: Called after initial LIST and when new object arrives\n- `OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{})`: Called on object change\n- `OnDelete(obj interface{})`: Called on deletion (object is the deleted version)\n\n**Resync Period**: Controls periodic re-notification\n- Default: 0 (disabled)\n- Can be per-handler\n- Useful for controllers that need to reconcile periodically\n\n**Design Guarantee**: Events for same object are delivered sequentially; events for different objects can interleave.\n\n---\n\n### 2.4 Listers (`listers/`)\n\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/listers/`\n\n**Responsibility**: Thread-safe, read-only accessor to the informer's cache for controllers.\n\n**Generated Interfaces** (`listers/[group]/[version]/[resource].go`):\n```go\ntype PodLister interface {\n    List(selector labels.Selector) ([]*v1.Pod, error)\n    Pods(namespace string) PodNamespaceLister\n}\n\ntype PodNamespaceLister interface {\n    List(selector labels.Selector) ([]*v1.Pod, error)\n    Get(name string) (*v1.Pod, error)\n}\n```\n\n**Key Design**:\n- No mutation methods (thread-safe reads only)\n- Uses informer's Indexer under the hood\n- Supports namespace-scoped and cluster-wide queries\n- Label selector filtering\n\n**Pattern Usage**:\n```go\n// In controller reconciliation\npod, err := podLister.Pods(namespace).Get(name)\n// Direct cache read; no API call\n```\n\n**Design Trade-off**: Eventual consistency\u2014pod might be deleted on server but still in cache briefly.\n\n---\n\n### 2.5 Work Queue (`util/workqueue/`)\n\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/`\n\n**Responsibility**: FIFO queue with rate limiting for decoupling event detection from processing.\n\n**Interfaces**:\n```go\ntype TypedInterface[T comparable] interface {\n    Add(item T)\n    Get() (item T, shutdown bool)\n    Done(item T)\n    ShutDown()\n}\n\ntype TypedRateLimitingInterface[T comparable] interface {\n    AddRateLimited(item T)  // After rate limit allows\n    Forget(item T)           // Reset retry count\n    NumRequeues(item T) int\n}\n```\n\n**Rate Limiter Types**:\n- **ExponentialBackoff**: 1ms, 2ms, 4ms, 8ms, ... up to max\n- **LinearBackoff**: Similar progression, linear increments\n- **BucketRateLimiter**: Token bucket (QPS-based)\n- **ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter**: Per-item retry tracking\n\n**Typical Controller Loop**:\n```go\n// Event handler\nif err := wq.Add(key); err != nil {\n    // log error\n}\n\n// Controller loop\nfor {\n    key, shutdown := wq.Get()\n    if shutdown { break }\n\n    if err := reconcile(key); err != nil {\n        wq.AddRateLimited(key)  // Retry with backoff\n    } else {\n        wq.Forget(key)          // Success, reset backoff\n    }\n    wq.Done(key)\n}\n```\n\n**Design Pattern**: Informers \u2192 key (string) \u2192 WorkQueue \u2192 Process func\n- Decouple event detection (fast) from reconciliation (slow)\n- Handle transient errors without blocking\n- Prevent thundering herd on controller startup\n\n**Metrics**: Integration with `tools/metrics` for instrumentation\n- Queue length, processing latency, retries\n- Crucial for observability\n\n---\n\n### 2.6 Dynamic Client (`dynamic/`)\n\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/dynamic/`\n\n**Responsibility**: Generic, unstructured client for any Kubernetes resource (CRDs, built-ins, etc.).\n\n**Key Interfaces**:\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    Resource(resource schema.GroupVersionResource) NamespaceableResourceInterface\n}\n\ntype ResourceInterface interface {\n    Create(ctx context.Context, obj *unstructured.Unstructured, ...) (*unstructured.Unstructured, error)\n    Get(ctx context.Context, name string, ...) (*unstructured.Unstructured, error)\n    List(ctx context.Context, opts metav1.ListOptions) (*unstructured.UnstructuredList, error)\n    Update(ctx context.Context, obj *unstructured.Unstructured, ...) (*unstructured.Unstructured, error)\n    Patch(ctx context.Context, name string, pt types.PatchType, data []byte, ...) (*unstructured.Unstructured, error)\n    Apply(ctx context.Context, name string, obj *unstructured.Unstructured, ...) (*unstructured.Unstructured, error)\n}\n```\n\n**Use Case**: Working with unstructured objects or custom resources\n```go\ngvr := schema.GroupVersionResource{Group: \"example.com\", Version: \"v1\", Resource: \"widgets\"}\nunstructured := &unstructured.Unstructured{Object: map[string]interface{}{\"metadata\": map[string]interface{}{\"name\": \"my-widget\"}}}\nresult, err := dynamicClient.Resource(gvr).Namespace(\"default\").Create(ctx, unstructured, metav1.CreateOptions{})\n```\n\n**Dynamic Informers** (`dynamic/dynamicinformer/`):\n- Use unstructured objects with informer machinery\n- Requires REST mapper to resolve GVK \u2192 REST path\n\n**Comparison with Typed Client**:\n| Aspect | Typed | Dynamic |\n|--------|-------|---------|\n| Type Safety | Compile-time | Runtime |\n| Discovery | None (generated) | Via REST mapper |\n| Flexibility | Low (one client per API group) | High (any resource) |\n| CRD Support | After code generation | Automatic |\n| Performance | Slightly faster (no reflection) | Slightly slower |\n\n---\n\n### 2.7 Metadata Client (`metadata/`)\n\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/metadata/`\n\n**Responsibility**: Lightweight client working only with object metadata (PartialObjectMetadata).\n\n**Use Case**: Operations requiring only metadata (labels, ownerReferences, status.observedGeneration)\n```go\nmetadataClient.Resource(gvr).Namespace(\"default\").Get(ctx, name, metav1.GetOptions{})\n// Returns *metav1.PartialObjectMetadata, not full object\n```\n\n**Benefits**:\n- Reduced bandwidth (metadata only)\n- Efficient for label-based filtering\n- Suitable for garbage collection and owner reference tracking\n\n---\n\n### 2.8 Discovery Client (`discovery/`)\n\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/discovery/`\n\n**Responsibility**: Querying API server for supported groups, versions, and resource metadata.\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `ServerGroups()`: List all API groups\n- `ServerResourcesForGroupVersion(groupVersion string)`: List resources in a group\n- `OpenAPISchema()`: Fetch OpenAPI v2 or v3 schema\n- `ServerPreferredResources()`: List preferred versions only\n\n**Implementation Detail**: Uses `/api`, `/apis`, and `/openapi/*` endpoints\n\n**Caching**:\n- `CachedDiscoveryClient` wraps DiscoveryClient\n- Caches group/version info in files (`~/.kube/cache/discovery/...`)\n- Invalidates on version mismatch\n\n**REST Mapper** (`restmapper/`):\n- Builds mapping: Kind \u2192 REST path\n- Uses discovery under the hood\n- Expensive operation (avoid in tight loops)\n\n**Design Trade-off**: Discovery overhead on startup; use cached version in production\n\n---\n\n### 2.9 Config and Authentication (`rest/config.go`, `tools/clientcmd/`, `transport/`)\n\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/rest/`, `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/clientcmd/`, `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/transport/`\n\n**Responsibility**: Build and configure HTTP clients with proper authentication.\n\n**Config Building Patterns**:\n1. **In-Cluster** (`rest.InClusterConfig()`): Auto-detect from Pod environment\n   - Token: `/var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/token`\n   - CA: `/var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/ca.crt`\n   - Host: `KUBERNETES_SERVICE_HOST` environment variable\n\n2. **Kubeconfig** (`clientcmd.BuildConfigFromFlags()`): Parse `~/.kube/config` or custom path\n   - Multiple contexts, clusters, users\n   - Supports exec-based and plugin-based auth\n\n3. **Manual**: Set fields directly on `rest.Config`\n\n**Authentication Layers** (RoundTripper chain, `transport/round_trippers.go`):\n- Bearer token wrapper: Adds `Authorization: Bearer <token>` header\n- Basic auth wrapper: Base64-encodes credentials\n- Impersonation wrapper: Adds `Impersonate-*` headers for admin operations\n- User-Agent wrapper: Identifies the client\n- Custom wrappers via `Config.WrapTransport`\n\n**TLS Configuration**:\n- Client certificates (`CertFile`, `KeyFile`)\n- CA bundle (`CAFile`)\n- Server name for SNI (`ServerName`)\n- Insecure skip verify (`Insecure`)\n\n**Design Pattern**: Middleware chain of RoundTripper implementations\n- Each adds one concern (auth, logging, metrics, etc.)\n- Composable and testable\n\n---\n\n### 2.10 Leader Election (`tools/leaderelection/`)\n\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/`\n\n**Responsibility**: Distributed lock for single-replica operation across multiple instances.\n\n**Mechanism**:\n1. Controllers create or update a Lease object in API server\n2. Lease has `spec.holderIdentity` (pod name) and `spec.leaseRenewalTime`\n3. Multiple instances compete; only one holds the lock\n4. Lock holder updates Lease within `renewDeadline`\n5. On loss, controller shuts down gracefully\n\n**Configuration**:\n- `LeaseDuration`: How long lock is held (default 15s)\n- `RenewDeadline`: Deadline for renewing before expiry (default 10s)\n- `RetryPeriod`: How often to retry acquiring lock (default 2s)\n\n**Callbacks**:\n```go\nleaderelection.LeaderCallbacks{\n    OnStartedLeading: func(ctx context.Context) { /* run controller */ },\n    OnStoppedLeading: func() { /* cleanup */ },\n    OnNewLeader: func(identity string) { /* log new leader */ },\n}\n```\n\n**Design Pattern**: Graceful shutdown\n- On lease loss, context cancels\n- Controller should watch context and exit\n- New leader can start fresh with clean state\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control/Request Flows\n\n### 3.1 Simple One-Off API Call\n\n**Scenario**: Direct REST query without caching (e.g., checking current cluster status)\n\n**Code Path**:\n```\n1. rest.InClusterConfig() or clientcmd.BuildConfigFromFlags()\n   \u2514\u2500> Returns *rest.Config with auth, TLS, rate limiting\n\n2. kubernetes.NewForConfig(config)\n   \u2514\u2500> Constructs Clientset with RESTClient for each API group\n\n3. clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-pod\", metav1.GetOptions{})\n   \u2514\u2500> Typed client calls RESTClient.Verb(\"GET\").Resource(\"pods\").Name(\"my-pod\").Do(ctx)\n\n4. RESTClient.Do()\n   \u251c\u2500> Acquire rate limit token (flowcontrol.RateLimiter)\n   \u251c\u2500> Build HTTP request with auth headers (transport RoundTripper chain)\n   \u251c\u2500> Execute HTTP request to /api/v1/namespaces/default/pods/my-pod\n   \u251c\u2500> Handle 200: decode response into *v1.Pod\n   \u251c\u2500> Handle 404: return *errors.StatusError (Kubernetes API error)\n   \u251c\u2500> Handle 429: wait and retry (respecting Retry-After header)\n   \u2514\u2500> Return result or error\n\n5. Return &Pod{...}\n```\n\n**Reference Code**:\n- `rest/client.go:RESTClient.Do()`: Executes request\n- `rest/request.go:Request.Do()`: Builder pattern execution\n- `rest/request.go:request.transformResponse()`: Response handling\n- `transport/round_trippers.go`: Auth and retry logic\n\n**Performance**: Single round-trip to API server; no caching\n\n---\n\n### 3.2 Event-Driven Controller with Informer and Work Queue\n\n**Scenario**: Respond to Pod changes in real-time (typical operator use case)\n\n**Architecture**:\n```\nAPI Server (truth)\n    \u2193 (LIST + WATCH)\nReflector (polling)\n    \u2193\nDeltaFIFO (delta queue)\n    \u2193\nIndexer (cache)\n    \u2193\nEvent Handler \u2192 WorkQueue\n    \u2193\nController Loop \u2192 Reconcile\n    \u2193 (GET, UPDATE, PATCH, DELETE)\nAPI Server (write)\n```\n\n**Code Flow**:\n\n**Setup Phase** (before controller starts):\n```go\n// 1. Create informer factory\nfactory := informers.NewSharedInformerFactory(clientset, 15 * time.Minute)\n\n// 2. Create informer for Pods\npodInformer := factory.Core().V1().Pods()\n\n// 3. Register event handler\npodInformer.Informer().AddEventHandler(cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n    AddFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n        pod := obj.(*corev1.Pod)\n        workqueue.Add(fmt.Sprintf(\"%s/%s\", pod.Namespace, pod.Name))\n    },\n    UpdateFunc: func(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n        pod := newObj.(*corev1.Pod)\n        workqueue.Add(fmt.Sprintf(\"%s/%s\", pod.Namespace, pod.Name))\n    },\n    DeleteFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n        pod := obj.(*corev1.Pod)\n        workqueue.Add(fmt.Sprintf(\"%s/%s\", pod.Namespace, pod.Name))\n    },\n})\n\n// 4. Get lister for efficient reads\npodLister := podInformer.Lister()\n\n// 5. Start factory (runs all informers in background)\nfactory.Start(ctx.Done())\n\n// 6. Wait for initial LIST to complete\nif !cache.WaitForCacheSync(ctx.Done(), podInformer.Informer().HasSynced) {\n    return fmt.Errorf(\"failed to sync cache\")\n}\n```\n\n**Background Sync** (in goroutine, automatic):\n```\n1. Reflector.Run()\n   \u251c\u2500> LIST with resourceVersion=\"\"\n   \u2502   \u2514\u2500> HTTP GET /api/v1/pods (all namespaces)\n   \u2502       \u2514\u2500> API server returns ~1000 items in chunks\n   \u2502\n   \u251c\u2500> For each item: DeltaFIFO.Add(pod) // generates Delta{Added, pod}\n   \u2502\n   \u2514\u2500> Once LIST complete: DeltaFIFO.Replace([], rv) // generates Sync deltas for resync\n\n   \u2514\u2500> WATCH with resourceVersion=lastRV\n       \u2514\u2500> HTTP GET /api/v1/pods?watch=true&resourceVersion=12345\n           \u251c\u2500> Pod created: ADDED event \u2192 DeltaFIFO.Add() \u2192 Delta{Added, pod}\n           \u251c\u2500> Pod modified: MODIFIED event \u2192 DeltaFIFO.Update() \u2192 Delta{Updated, pod}\n           \u251c\u2500> Pod deleted: DELETED event \u2192 DeltaFIFO.Delete() \u2192 Delta{Deleted, pod}\n           \u2514\u2500> Watch timeout/error \u2192 Backoff and re-LIST\n\n2. DeltaFIFO.Pop() loop (internal to sharedIndexInformer)\n   \u251c\u2500> Get next delta from queue\n   \u2514\u2500> For each delta type (Added, Updated, Deleted, Sync):\n       \u251c\u2500> Update Indexer (cache)\n       \u2514\u2500> Call registered event handlers sequentially\n\n3. Event Handler callback\n   \u251c\u2500> Extract pod key: \"default/my-pod\"\n   \u2514\u2500> workqueue.Add(\"default/my-pod\")\n```\n\n**Reference Code**:\n- `tools/cache/reflector.go:Reflector.ListAndWatch()`: LIST/WATCH protocol\n- `tools/cache/delta_fifo.go:DeltaFIFO.Pop()`: Process deltas\n- `tools/cache/shared_informer.go:sharedIndexInformer.Run()`: Orchestration\n\n**Controller Reconciliation Loop** (user code):\n```go\nfunc(c *Controller) Run(ctx context.Context, workers int) error {\n    // Spawn worker goroutines\n    for i := 0; i < workers; i++ {\n        go c.worker(ctx)\n    }\n    <-ctx.Done()\n    return nil\n}\n\nfunc(c *Controller) worker(ctx context.Context) {\n    for {\n        key, shutdown := c.workqueue.Get()\n        if shutdown {\n            return\n        }\n\n        if err := c.syncHandler(ctx, key); err != nil {\n            c.workqueue.AddRateLimited(key)  // Retry with exponential backoff\n            klog.Error(err, \"Reconcile error\", \"key\", key)\n        } else {\n            c.workqueue.Forget(key)  // Success, reset backoff\n        }\n        c.workqueue.Done(key)\n    }\n}\n\nfunc(c *Controller) syncHandler(ctx context.Context, key string) error {\n    namespace, name, err := cache.SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)\n    if err != nil {\n        return err\n    }\n\n    // Read from cache (fast, no API call)\n    pod, err := c.podLister.Pods(namespace).Get(name)\n    if apierrors.IsNotFound(err) {\n        // Pod was deleted, cleanup if needed\n        return nil\n    }\n    if err != nil {\n        return err  // Real error, will be requeued\n    }\n\n    // Reconciliation logic\n    if !pod.Status.Ready {\n        // Take action (e.g., trigger pod recreation)\n        // Use clientset to issue API calls\n        if err := c.clientset.CoreV1().Pods(namespace).Delete(ctx, name, metav1.DeleteOptions{}); err != nil {\n            return err\n        }\n    }\n\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\n**Reference Code**:\n- Example: `/workspace/examples/workqueue/` (if present)\n- `tools/cache/shared_informer.go`: Guarantees\n\n**Critical Guarantees**:\n1. **Sequential per-object**: If Pod \"default/my-pod\" changes 3 times, event handler is called 3 times in order\n2. **Eventual consistency**: Cache will eventually match API server (barring network partitions)\n3. **At-least-once semantics**: Event handler will be called; may be called again on resync\n\n**Trade-off**: Informer setup overhead (~1 minute to populate for 10k objects) but efficient incremental updates thereafter.\n\n---\n\n### 3.3 Server-Side Apply (Declarative Updates)\n\n**Scenario**: Multiple controllers need to manage the same object declaratively (e.g., workload infrastructure)\n\n**Code Flow**:\n```go\n// Generated apply configuration type (type-safe)\ndeploymentApplyConfig := appsv1apply.Deployment(\"my-deployment\", \"default\").\n    WithSpec(appsv1apply.DeploymentSpec().\n        WithReplicas(3).\n        WithSelector(metav1.SetAsMapOfStringString(map[string]string{\"app\": \"myapp\"})).\n        WithTemplate(corev1apply.PodTemplateSpec().\n            WithSpec(corev1apply.PodSpec().\n                WithContainers(corev1apply.Container().\n                    WithName(\"myapp\").\n                    WithImage(\"myimage:v1.0\")))))\n\n// Apply to API server\nresult, err := clientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").Apply(\n    ctx,\n    deploymentApplyConfig,\n    metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"my-controller\"},\n)\n```\n\n**Key Difference from CRUD**:\n- **CRUD (Create/Update)**: Replace entire object; multiple controllers conflict\n- **Apply**: Server-side merge; multiple controllers can coexist\n  - Each controller specifies `FieldManager` identity\n  - Server tracks which fields each controller owns\n  - On update, server merges all field owners' contributions\n\n**API Interaction**:\n```\n1. Client builds FieldSet (fields being managed)\n2. Client sends PATCH request with Content-Type: application/apply-patch+json\n3. API server:\n   - Unmarshals patch\n   - Merges with current object\n   - Updates FieldManager metadata\n   - Validates merged result\n   - Returns merged object\n```\n\n**Reference Code**:\n- `applyconfigurations/`: Generated type-safe builders\n- `rest/request.go:Request.Apply()`: PATCH implementation\n\n**Design Trade-off**: Slightly slower than direct PATCH (merge overhead) but enables multi-controller safety.\n\n---\n\n### 3.4 Discovery and REST Mapping\n\n**Scenario**: Tool needs to work with arbitrary resource types (CRDs, future APIs)\n\n**Code Flow**:\n```go\n// 1. Discover available APIs\ndiscoveryClient, _ := discovery.NewDiscoveryClientForConfig(config)\napiGroups, _ := discoveryClient.ServerGroups()  // HTTP GET /apis\n\n// 2. Get resources for a specific group version\nresources, _ := discoveryClient.ServerResourcesForGroupVersion(\"mygroup.io/v1\")\n// HTTP GET /apis/mygroup.io/v1\n\n// 3. Build REST mapper\nrestMapper := restmapper.NewDeferredDiscoveryRESTMapper(discoveryClient)\n\n// 4. Map Kind to REST resource\nmapping, _ := restMapper.RESTMapping(schema.GroupKind{\n    Group: \"mygroup.io\",\n    Kind:  \"Widget\",\n})\n// Internally calls discovery if not cached\n// Returns: GroupVersion: mygroup.io/v1, Resource: \"widgets\"\n\n// 5. Use dynamic client with resolved resource\ngvr := mapping.Resource\ndynamicClient, _ := dynamic.NewForConfig(config)\nlist, _ := dynamicClient.Resource(gvr).List(ctx, metav1.ListOptions{})\n```\n\n**Performance Implications**:\n- Discovery cached locally (in memory and on disk)\n- REST mapper caches mappings\n- First call: slow (multiple HTTP requests)\n- Subsequent calls: fast (cached)\n\n**Reference Code**:\n- `discovery/discovery_client.go:DiscoveryClient.ServerGroups()`: API group discovery\n- `restmapper/discovery.go`: REST mapping logic\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Trade-Offs\n\n### 4.1 Network and Connectivity Failures\n\n**Failure Mode**: API server unreachable, slow, or intermittently failing\n\n**Client Behavior**:\n1. **Rate Limiting**: Respects `Retry-After` headers from 429 (Too Many Requests)\n2. **Backoff**: Exponential backoff on 5xx errors\n   - Base: 1 second, Max: ~30 seconds by default\n   - Configurable via `KUBE_CLIENT_BACKOFF_BASE` and `KUBE_CLIENT_BACKOFF_DURATION`\n\n3. **Watch Timeout**: If watch stream idle for 5+ minutes, reconnect\n   - `defaultMinWatchTimeout = 5 * time.Minute` (randomized)\n   - Prevents connection leaks on proxy timeouts\n\n4. **\"Too Old\" Recovery**: If resourceVersion is too old (stale)\n   - Reflector detects 410 Gone\n   - Falls back to new LIST operation\n   - Prevents infinite watch hangs\n\n**Implication**: Controllers may experience lag (cache 5+ minutes behind API server during outages) but will eventually catch up.\n\n**Observability**:\n- Logs: Backoff delays, watch reconnects\n- Metrics: API request latency, rate limit saturation, queue depth\n\n---\n\n### 4.2 Stale Cache Window\n\n**Failure Mode**: Controller acts on old information\n\n**Scenario**:\n1. Pod ready at time T1\n2. Pod crashes at time T2\n3. Informer cache reflects crash at time T3 (T3 > T1)\n4. Controller reconciles between T2 and T3 on stale data\n\n**Mitigations**:\n1. **Periodic Resync**: Full cache reconciliation every 15 minutes (default)\n   - Detects drift from API server\n   - Triggers re-reconciliation of all objects\n\n2. **Idempotent Reconciliation**: Controllers should be safe to run multiple times\n   - Check actual state, not assumed state\n   - Compare desired vs. current\n\n3. **Owner References**: Use for tracking object dependencies\n   - If pod deleted, cascade via ownerReferences\n   - Avoids relying on single object state\n\n**Trade-off**: Resync period balances drift detection (short) vs. API server load (long)\n\n---\n\n### 4.3 Resource Version Confusion\n\n**Failure Mode**: Controller loses track of sync position\n\n**Scenario**:\n1. Pod resourceVersion: 12345\n2. Controller crashes\n3. Restart: informer doesn't know where it was\n4. Reflector starts LIST with resourceVersion=\"\" (full resync)\n\n**Design**: Informers don't persist resourceVersion\n- Intentional: Simplified state management\n- Trade-off: Every restart does full LIST\n\n**Implication**: Large clusters (1000+ pods) may spike API server load on controller restart\n\n---\n\n### 4.4 Mutation Race Conditions\n\n**Failure Mode**: Multiple controllers write to same object, conflicts occur\n\n**Conflict Scenarios**:\n1. **Two clients update simultaneously**:\n   - Client A reads Pod, modifies, writes (resourceVersion 100)\n   - Client B reads Pod, modifies, writes (resourceVersion 100)\n   - Second write fails: 409 Conflict\n\n2. **Two clients apply simultaneously**:\n   - Both use server-side apply with different FieldManagers\n   - Server merges changes\n   - Both succeed (eventual consistency)\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Use work queue with rate limiting (prevents thundering herd)\n- Use leader election for single-writer models\n- Use server-side apply for multi-writer models\n\n**Reference Code**:\n- `tools/leaderelection/`: Single-writer pattern\n\n---\n\n### 4.5 Cache Size and Memory\n\n**Concern**: Large clusters with many objects\n\n**Scenario**: Cluster with 10,000 Deployments \u00d7 10 fields each = millions of objects in memory\n\n**Mitigations**:\n1. **Selector Restrictions**: Informers support label/field selectors\n   ```go\n   podInformer := factory.Core().V1().Pods().Informer()\n   // Cache only pods in namespace \"default\"\n   // Requires TweakListOptions customization\n   ```\n\n2. **Metadata-Only Informers**: Use metadata client to cache only object metadata\n   ```go\n   metadataInformer := informers.NewMetadataSharedInformerFactory(metadataClient, 15 * time.Minute)\n   ```\n\n3. **Lazy Loading**: Don't cache all resources; query API as needed\n   - Trade-off: Slower reads, lower memory\n\n4. **Index Pruning**: Only create indexes for actually used fields\n   ```go\n   indexer.AddIndexers(map[string]cache.IndexFunc{\n       \"ownerReference\": indexOwnerReferences,\n       // Not: every field\n   })\n   ```\n\n**Design Trade-off**: Cached informers use more memory but provide fast access; trade off for large deployments.\n\n---\n\n### 4.6 Watch Stream Pressure (Backpressure)\n\n**Failure Mode**: Event handler blocks, work queue backs up\n\n**Scenario**:\n1. API server sends 1000 Pod updates rapidly\n2. Event handler slow (takes 1 second per Pod)\n3. DeltaFIFO queue backs up\n4. Informer can't process deletions\n5. Leaked resources\n\n**Mitigations**:\n1. **Fast Event Handlers**: Just queue the key; don't process inline\n   ```go\n   AddFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n       key, _ := cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)  // ~1 microsecond\n       workqueue.Add(key)                         // ~1 millisecond\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Worker Pool**: Multiple goroutines processing work queue\n   - Default: 1 worker (can be tuned)\n   - Each gets independent copy of work\n\n3. **Watch Bookmarks**: Allows efficient recovery without LIST\n   - Reduces pressure on API server\n\n**Design Guarantee**: Event handler blocking doesn't block future events (sequential per-object, not global)\n\n---\n\n### 4.7 Informer Synchronization Window\n\n**Concern**: When is informer cache guaranteed to be synced?\n\n**Guarantee**:\n```go\nHasSynced() bool  // True after initial LIST completes\n```\n\n**Window**:\n- Creation: empty cache\n- Initial LIST: populating from API\n- HasSynced(): true (not yet, but immediately after)\n- First WATCH event arrival: fully synced\n\n**Implication**: Between start and HasSynced, queries return incomplete results\n\n**Mitigation**:\n```go\nif !cache.WaitForCacheSync(ctx.Done(), informer.HasSynced) {\n    return fmt.Errorf(\"cache not synced\")\n}\n// Now safe to query\n```\n\n---\n\n### 4.8 Deletion Race: Object Deleted Before Processing\n\n**Failure Mode**: Controller tries to process deleted object\n\n**Scenario**:\n1. Pod deleted on API server\n2. Deletion event queued in work queue\n3. Controller tries to GET pod by name\n4. Pod is gone; GET returns 404 NotFound\n\n**Controller Code**:\n```go\npod, err := c.podLister.Pods(namespace).Get(name)\nif apierrors.IsNotFound(err) {\n    // Expected; pod was deleted\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\n**Design Guarantee**: DeleteFunc receives last known state of object\n```go\nDeleteFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n    pod := obj.(*corev1.Pod)  // Pod object with data, not nil\n    // Can access pod.OwnerReferences, pod.Finalizers, etc.\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 5.1 Custom Indexes for Efficient Queries\n\n**Use Case**: Look up Pods by owner, by node, by service\n\n**Pattern**:\n```go\n// Define index function\nfunc indexPodByNode(obj interface{}) ([]string, error) {\n    pod := obj.(*corev1.Pod)\n    if pod.Spec.NodeName == \"\" {\n        return []string{}, nil\n    }\n    return []string{pod.Spec.NodeName}, nil\n}\n\n// Register with informer\npodInformer.Informer().GetIndexer().AddIndexers(map[string]cache.IndexFunc{\n    \"nodeName\": indexPodByNode,\n})\n\n// Query\npods, err := podInformer.Informer().GetIndexer().ByIndex(\"nodeName\", \"node-1\")\n```\n\n**Reference Code**: `tools/cache/indexer.go`\n\n**Risk**: Custom indexes consume memory; don't index every field\n\n---\n\n### 5.2 Custom RoundTripper for Auth/Logging\n\n**Use Case**: Add custom authentication, trace requests, rate limit per-tenant\n\n**Pattern**:\n```go\nconfig := &rest.Config{\n    Host: \"...\",\n    // ...\n    WrapTransport: func(rt http.RoundTripper) http.RoundTripper {\n        return &customRoundTripper{wrapped: rt}\n    },\n}\n\ntype customRoundTripper struct {\n    wrapped http.RoundTripper\n}\n\nfunc (r *customRoundTripper) RoundTrip(req *http.Request) (*http.Response, error) {\n    // Log request\n    log.Printf(\"Request: %s %s\", req.Method, req.URL)\n\n    // Add custom header\n    req.Header.Add(\"X-Custom-Header\", \"value\")\n\n    // Delegate\n    return r.wrapped.RoundTrip(req)\n}\n```\n\n**Reference Code**: `transport/round_trippers.go`\n\n**Risk**: Custom wrappers can block or panic; test thoroughly\n\n---\n\n### 5.3 Custom Event Handlers and Filtering\n\n**Use Case**: Only reconcile certain objects, batch events\n\n**Pattern**:\n```go\n// Filter to only certain namespaces\nhandler := cache.FilteringResourceEventHandler{\n    FilterFunc: func(obj interface{}) bool {\n        pod := obj.(*corev1.Pod)\n        return pod.Namespace == \"my-namespace\"\n    },\n    Handler: cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n        AddFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n            // Only called for pods in \"my-namespace\"\n            key, _ := cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n            workqueue.Add(key)\n        },\n    },\n}\n\npodInformer.Informer().AddEventHandler(handler)\n```\n\n**Reference Code**: `tools/cache/shared_informer.go`\n\n**Risk**: Filtering reduces events; ensure no critical objects are filtered out\n\n---\n\n### 5.4 Custom Store Transformations\n\n**Use Case**: Clean sensitive data, normalize object state before caching\n\n**Pattern**:\n```go\ntransformFunc := func(obj interface{}) (interface{}, error) {\n    pod := obj.(*corev1.Pod)\n    // Clear environment variables (sensitive)\n    for i := range pod.Spec.Containers {\n        pod.Spec.Containers[i].Env = nil\n    }\n    return pod, nil\n}\n\nconfig := &Config{\n    DeltaFIFOOptions: cache.DeltaFIFOOptions{\n        Transformer: transformFunc,\n    },\n}\n```\n\n**Reference Code**: `tools/cache/delta_fifo.go:TransformFunc`\n\n**Risk**: Transformation drops data; subsequent reads won't have full object\n\n---\n\n### 5.5 Custom Clients via Factory Patterns\n\n**Use Case**: Inject mocked or custom clients for testing\n\n**Pattern**:\n```go\ntype fakeClientset struct {\n    // Mock methods\n}\n\nfunc (f *fakeClientset) CoreV1() corev1.CoreV1Interface {\n    return &fakeCoreV1Client{}\n}\n\n// Inject in controller\ncontroller.clientset = &fakeClientset{}\n```\n\n**Reference Code**: `kubernetes/fake/` (code-generated fake implementations)\n\n**Leverage**: Code generation provides fake clients automatically\n\n---\n\n### 5.6 Leader Election with Custom Locks\n\n**Use Case**: Use different lock backends (etcd, database) instead of Lease\n\n**Pattern**:\n```go\ntype CustomLock struct {\n    client resourcelock.Interface\n    LockConfig resourcelock.ResourceLockConfig\n}\n\nfunc (c *CustomLock) Get(ctx context.Context) (*resourcelock.LeaderElectionRecord, []byte, error) {\n    // Read from custom backend\n}\n\nfunc (c *CustomLock) Create(ctx context.Context, ler resourcelock.LeaderElectionRecord) error {\n    // Write to custom backend\n}\n\nfunc (c *CustomLock) Update(ctx context.Context, ler resourcelock.LeaderElectionRecord, raw []byte) error {\n    // Update custom backend\n}\n\nleaderelection.RunOrDie(ctx, leaderelection.LeaderElectionConfig{\n    Lock: &CustomLock{...},\n    // ...\n})\n```\n\n**Reference Code**: `tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/`\n\n**Risk**: Custom locks must be highly available and consistent; bugs cause all replicas to run\n\n---\n\n### 5.7 Custom Rate Limiter Strategies\n\n**Use Case**: Exponential backoff, linear backoff, or custom logic\n\n**Pattern**:\n```go\ntype customRateLimiter struct{\n    itemRetries map[string]int\n}\n\nfunc (c *customRateLimiter) When(item interface{}) time.Duration {\n    key := item.(string)\n    retries := c.itemRetries[key]\n    // Custom logic: e.g., different backoff for transient vs. permanent errors\n    return time.Duration(retries*retries) * time.Second\n}\n\nwq := workqueue.NewTypedRateLimitingQueue(customRateLimiter{...})\n```\n\n**Reference Code**: `util/workqueue/rate_limiter.go`\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n**API Server Load**:\n- **LIST operation**: O(num_objects) time, O(num_objects) memory on server\n  - Happens on informer start, per REST mapper initialization, full resync\n  - Typical: 100 Pods = 1 HTTP request, 1000 Pods = chunked requests\n\n- **WATCH operation**: O(1) per change, streaming connection\n  - Efficient; server filters events per watch\n  - Typical: 1 event = 1 HTTP frame\n\n- **Avoid**: Unbounded queries without selectors (e.g., `List(ctx, metav1.ListOptions{})` for all namespaces)\n  - Use `Pods(v1.NamespaceAll)` with explicit namespace awareness\n\n**Controller Load**:\n- Work queue processing: O(1) per item (amortized)\n- Lister queries: O(log n) with indexes, O(n) without\n- Reconciliation: Controller-dependent\n\n**Memory Usage**:\n- Per object cached: ~1 KB (Pod metadata) to ~100 KB (full definition)\n- Per index: ~1 KB per object entry\n- Per watch connection: ~1 MB (buffer)\n\n**Benchmarks**: (Rough guidance)\n- 100 objects: <1 MB, ~10 ms latency\n- 1000 objects: ~100 MB, ~50 ms latency\n- 10,000 objects: ~1 GB, ~500 ms latency\n\n---\n\n### 6.2 Observability and Metrics\n\n**Built-in Metrics** (via `tools/metrics/`):\n- `apiserver_request_duration_seconds`: REST client latency\n- `apiserver_request_total`: Request count by verb, resource\n- `apiserver_request_content_type`: Content negotiation usage\n- `apiserver_client_certificate_expiration_seconds`: cert expiry tracking\n- `workqueue_depth`: Items in work queue\n- `workqueue_adds_total`: Items enqueued\n- `workqueue_processing_seconds`: Processing latency per item\n- `workqueue_longest_running_processor_seconds`: Longest reconciliation time\n- `workqueue_unfinished_work_seconds`: Items taking longer than timeout\n\n**Logging**:\n- `-v 2`: REST client requests and responses\n- `-v 4`: Detailed rate limiter logs\n- `-v 6`: Request/response bodies (enable via klog)\n\n**Tracing**:\n- `net/http/httptrace` integration\n- Trace key points: DNS lookup, TLS handshake, TTFB\n\n**How to Observe**:\n```bash\n# Check API server load\nkubectl get --raw=/metrics | grep apiserver_request\n\n# Check controller health\nkubectl get --raw=/metrics | grep workqueue\n\n# View verbose logs\ncontroller --v=2\n```\n\n---\n\n### 6.3 Scaling Considerations\n\n**Single Controller**:\n- Recommended: <1000 objects\n- Bottleneck: Reconciliation latency (depends on user code)\n\n**Multiple Controllers**:\n- Use leader election for coordinated operations\n- Each controller has independent work queue\n- Total API server load = sum of all controllers\n\n**Large Clusters**:\n- Use selector restrictions (limit cache size)\n- Use metadata-only informers\n- Consider custom storage backends for frequently accessed objects\n\n**HA Setup**:\n```\n3 controller replicas\n  \u251c\u2500> Leader election via Lease\n  \u2514\u2500> Only 1 active; others standby\n  \u2514\u2500> On leader crash: election finishes in ~15s\n```\n\n---\n\n### 6.4 Failure Recovery and Resilience\n\n**Controller Crash**:\n1. Pod terminates\n2. New Pod starts (by Deployment)\n3. Informer re-LIST and re-WATCH\n4. Work queue reprocesses old events\n5. Duplicate reconciliation possible but idempotent (by design)\n\n**API Server Restart**:\n1. Clients see connection refused\n2. Backoff and retry\n3. Once available, continue (cache may be stale briefly)\n4. Full resync picks up any drift\n\n**Network Partition**:\n1. Clients timeout (watch idle > 5 minutes)\n2. Exponential backoff kicks in\n3. Once partition heals, recovery automatic\n4. Resync detects missed events\n\n**Mitigations**:\n- Run multiple controller replicas\n- Use leader election for safety\n- Implement idempotent reconciliation\n- Add health checks (query cache, monitor work queue depth)\n\n---\n\n### 6.5 Tuning Guidance\n\n**For High Latency (slow reconciliation)**:\n- Increase worker count (process more work queue items concurrently)\n- Reduce resync period (catch drift faster)\n- Use more specific selectors (reduce object count)\n\n**For High API Server Load**:\n- Increase resync period (less frequent reconciliation)\n- Use metadata-only informers\n- Batch reconciliation (process multiple items per loop)\n\n**For Memory Pressure**:\n- Use metadata-only informers\n- Limit cache to specific namespaces/selectors\n- Reduce number of indexes\n\n**For Stale Cache Issues**:\n- Reduce resync period (default 15 min)\n- Add explicit refresh on error\n- Use periodic validation (compare cache vs. API)\n\n---\n\n## 7. Critical Reference Map\n\nThis section maps key files for quick navigation during implementation or investigation.\n\n### 7.1 Core REST and Configuration\n\n| Component | Location | Responsibility Summary\n\n**Client-go Architecture**:\n1. **Foundation**: REST client with rate limiting and backoff\n2. **Type Safety**: Code-generated clients for all Kubernetes APIs\n3. **Efficiency**: Cached informers with event-driven synchronization\n4. **Operational**: Work queues, rate limiting, leader election\n5. **Flexibility**: Dynamic and metadata clients for untyped access\n\n**Key Strengths**:\n- Eventual consistency guarantees simplify controller logic\n- Event-driven reconciliation prevents polling overhead\n- Code generation ensures API server/client alignment\n- Work queues enable robust error handling\n\n**Key Constraints**:\n- Informers have startup cost (LIST all objects)\n- Cache eventual consistency window\n- Resync overhead on large object counts\n- Requires idempotent reconciliation logic\n\n**When to Use**:\n- **Typed Client**: Building in-tree controllers, working with stable APIs\n- **Informer**: Responsive controllers, distributed state management\n- **Dynamic Client**: Tools, CLIs, custom resource handling\n- **Metadata Client**: Efficient label-based operations\n- **REST Client**: One-off queries, diagnostics\n\nThis guide should provide sufficient context for extending client-go, understanding its failure modes, and making informed architecture decisions for Kubernetes-aware applications.\n",
